    <meta name="dc.description" content="The drumstick tree (Moringa oleifera Lam.) is a perennial crop that has gained popularity in certain developing countries for its high-nutrition content and adaptability to arid and semi-arid environments. Here we report a high-quality draft genome sequence of M. oleifera. This assembly represents 91.78% of the estimated genome size and contains 19,465 protein-coding genes. Comparative genomic analysis between M. oleifera and related woody plant genomes helps clarify the general evolution of this species, while the identification of several species-specific gene families and positively selected genes in M. oleifera may help identify genes related to M. oleifera&#8217;s high protein content, fast-growth, heat and stress tolerance. This reference genome greatly extends the basic research on M. oleifera, and may further promote applying genomics to enhanced breeding and improvement of M. oleifera."/>

        <meta property="og:url" content="https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s11427-015-4872-x"/>
        <meta property="og:type" content="article"/>
        <meta property="og:site_name" content="Science China Life Sciences"/>
        <meta property="og:title" content="High quality reference genome of drumstick tree ( Moringa oleifera Lam.), a potential perennial crop"/>
        <meta property="og:description" content="The drumstick tree (Moringa oleifera Lam.) is a perennial crop that has gained popularity in certain developing countries for its high-nutrition content and adaptability to arid and semi-arid environments. Here we report a high-quality draft genome sequence of M. oleifera. This assembly represents 91.78% of the estimated genome size and contains 19,465 protein-coding genes. Comparative genomic analysis between M. oleifera and related woody plant genomes helps clarify the general evolution of this species, while the identification of several species-specific gene families and positively selected genes in M. oleifera may help identify genes related to M. oleiferaâ€™s high protein content, fast-growth, heat and stress tolerance. This reference genome greatly extends the basic research on M. oleifera, and may further promote applying genomics to enhanced breeding and improvement of M. oleifera."/>
        <meta property="og:image" content="https://media.springernature.com/w200/springer-static/cover/journal/11427.jpg"/>

        function OptanonWrapper() {

                if (candidate === element) {
                    return true;
                } else if (candidate.nodeName.toLowerCase() === 'body') {
                    return false;
                } else {

            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };

                }

                return scriptEl;
            }

            for (var i = 0; i < headScripts.length; ++i) {
                var scriptEl = createScript(headScripts[i]);
                currentScript.parentNode.insertBefore(scriptEl, currentScript.nextSibling);
            }

            d.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
                for (var i = 0; i < bodyScripts.length; ++i) {
                    var scriptEl = createScript(bodyScripts[i]);
                    d.body.appendChild(scriptEl);
                }
            });

            // Webfont repeat view
            var config = w.config;
            if (config && config.publisherBrand && sessionStorage.fontsLoaded === 'true') {
                d.documentElement.className += ' webfonts-loaded';
            }
        })(window, document);
    }
</script>

                <div data-article-body="true" data-track-component="article body" class="c-article-body">
                    <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>The drumstick tree (<i>Moringa oleifera</i> Lam.) is a perennial crop that has gained popularity in certain developing countries for its high-nutrition content and adaptability to arid and semi-arid environments. Here we report a high-quality draft genome sequence of <i>M. oleifera</i>. This assembly represents 91.78% of the estimated genome size and contains 19,465 protein-coding genes. Comparative genomic analysis between <i>M. oleifera</i> and related woody plant genomes helps clarify the general evolution of this species, while the identification of several species-specific gene families and positively selected genes in <i>M. oleifera</i> may help identify genes related to <i>M. oleifera</i>â€™s high protein content, fast-growth, heat and stress tolerance. This reference genome greatly extends the basic research on <i>M. oleifera</i>, and may further promote applying genomics to enhanced breeding and improvement of <i>M. oleifera</i>.</p></div></div></section>
                    
    


                    

                    
    <div class="note test-pdf-link" id="cobranding-and-download-availability-text">
